    <li> Full results yet to be determined, which is why I currently give the product 3 stars.  I&#x27;ll update as I proceed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Day 1: Took a 30 minute hot bath with sea salt soak in order to prepare my feet.  I opened the package and cut open the bootie packets which were exactly as pictured.  There is a lavender smell but also something sharper and a bit stringent, which is not surprising.  Overall not a bad smell.  It was fairly unpleasant sliding my feet into cold jelly, and some liquid did ooze out the top, so I recommend having an old towel under your feet for the duration.  The tape that came with the booties to close them up around your ankles was completely useless, so I just slid on some old fuzzy socks and that held them on well enough.  Sat for an hour and then because the baby was sleeping, carefully made my way upstairs - NOT advised.  Very hard to walk.  I removed the booties and rinsed my feet very well in the tub - did not re-soak as I did not have time.  No lotion.  About four hours later my feet felt a bit puffy and kind of burned - as if I&#x27;d been walking on hot sand all day.  The skin also felt a bit itchy.  There was no redness and this feeling subsided by the time I went to bed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Day 2: Skin might look a little shiny, otherwise no change.  Stopped up the shower drain to soak feet while I showered.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Day 3: Now we&#x27;re talking...soaked my feet for 15 minutes after work and had large areas of shedding!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Day 4-5: Shedding continued in smaller amounts.  Not quite the huge sheets that previous reviews had led me to believe, but perhaps because I was not soaking (except day 3), just stopping up the shower drain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Days 6-8: This was the annoying part.  Itchy flaky skin on tops and sides of my feet, more irritating than anything else.  It was like a constant shower of tiny flakes any time I moved my feet, and was driving me crazy.  Finally took a pumice stone to it to end it because I was fed up.  At this point I also put lotion on the tops and sides of my feet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Verdict: Eh.  It was fun, interesting to see the process, but I don&#x27;t feel like the real problem areas got any more result than a particularly thorough pedicure would have.  I still have thick areas on the balls of my feet and heels.  Maybe if I try again and am aggressive with daily soaking but for now I&#x27;ll stick with pedicures. Rinsed my feet really well, dried them and went about my afternoon. It immediately felt like there was liquid trapped in the arches of my feet when I would walk. Weird, but not unbearable. That night I couldn&#x27;t sleep. My feet were so dry they felt like they were going to crack in half. I soaked them for 10 minutes and was finally able to go to bed. Day 2-14: My feet became insanely dry, even with soaking for 20+ minutes every night. Every crease in my foot was bright white. The balls of my feet turned into sandpaper. I felt my feet getting stuck to socks. It was terrible. Day 15: no sign of peeling and I couldn&#x27;t take my dry, scratchy feet anymore. I spent nearly 30 minutes on each foot with a pumice stone and even a callous shaver in some parts. I slathered them in lotion and put on socks. It made no difference. Day 16-19: more work with the pumice stone and more soaking in hot water. I bought Palmer&#x27;s cocoa butter (the wax like stuff, not the lotion) and began spreading a 1/4 inch thick smear of it all over my feet, wrapping them in plastic wrap, putting on socks and going to bed. Day 20: I was running errands for work and felt like something was stuck under my big toe. Nope. Nearly a week after they should have started to peel, the peeling began. More lotion and more soaking, but the skin didn&#x27;t really come off too much. Day 23-25: Finally some noticeable peeling, but we were spending the weekend away and walking a bunch. All of the new, soft skin was now going to become hard from miles of walk. Just great. Day 28: The tops of my feet started to peel and I looked diseased. Fun times. Day 30: My toes started to peel. More looking diseased. Day 32: In desperate need of a pedicure, I sucked up my embarrassment and went. My pedicure lady yelled at me telling me if I wanted softer feet I should have come to her and we could have tried different lotions. She told me I better never use this on my feet again. She also peeled another layer off all of my toes. Day 40: There are still spots that are peeling, mainly on the sides of my feet where the skin is thin to begin with and just doesn&#x27;t want to come off. It took my feet so long to peel that by the time all of the bottoms of my feet had peeled, there was a mix of new soft skin and new skin that had already begun to get dry, despite lotion.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I guess it worked, but to have my feet still peeling after almost 5 weeks and the fact that they barely stayed soft? It&#x27;s just not worth it.  I&#x27;ll stick with the cocoa butter/plastic wrap routine on top of my regular pedicures instead.ff too much.     <li> I have dinosaur feet.  I didn&#x27;t always have them but after returning from a Virgin Islands trip 10 years ago I began to notice my feet becoming really rough in spots (heel, lower side section of big toe and side of pinky toe).  I went to a podiatrist and she tested for fungus etc but found nothing.  So, my days of scraping and moisturizing and wearing socks to bed because I was embarrassed for my husband to accidentally touch my feet during the night began.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The best product I had found before I discovered a blurb in a magazine about Baby Foot was pure Shea Butter.  It was a daily process however and if I skipped a day I noticed it would take 3 days of constant use  to \\&quot;catch up\\&quot; with fairly smooth feet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I had read enough positive reviews of Baby Foot to decide to give it a try.  I was a bit leery of it being a Japanese product but then realized I was probably being paranoid because of radiation fears (yeah, that is a whole other story).  The product I received came from Liberta U.S.A. Inc. so I am guessing they are the U.S. distributor now for this Japanese product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The product I received came in the red box with American English print with a photo of a woman&#x27;s feet (not the photo of a leg shown on the red box here at Amazon currently).  It says Lavender scent on the front.  The instructions on the back say the booties will fit Woman size 4-12 and Men 4-13 (American I am assuming).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After reading all the inconsistent reviews of results I decided to compare the ingredients in the different packaging types and found differences.  Some of these differences were in ingredients themselves and some just in the order of the ingredients (we all know the listed order of the ingredients determines the percentage of the ingredient in the product).  I won&#x27;t go into all the different ingredients or order differences but I will compare here a couple of really noticeable differences in the Liberta USA Inc. product I received and the red box American text with the womans legs and her hand on her calf.  One of the first differences in MY box and the box shown here on Amazon is the ingredient Salicylic Acid.  Now we ladies all know that ingredient from our facial masks and creams.  It is a good ingredient (unless you have ultra sensitive skin or a condition such as Rosacea) to have in a product that promises to get rid of dead topical skin.  Amazon here lists it as ingredient number 9.  My box lists it as ingredient number 32!  In fact, there are so many oil and extract ingredients listed on MY red box list before ANY of the acids (with exception of the lactic acid) that it is clear that the U.S. distributed product is a completely different product than what the Japanese had originally produced.  I don&#x27;t know if this is because our FDA deemed the actual acid concentration too high for sale in the U.S. or if it is just because Americans are just economically dumb and will buy anything made more cheaply even if it is ineffective.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, that said, I opened the package and found two clear, thin, boxy booty bags.  The gel was visable inside.  I had to use scissors to cut the very top of the booties.  I cut the tops of the booties at the same time.  I recommend you cut and put on one at a time however because it could get messy.  I was very careful and inserted each foot.  I didn&#x27;t notice any type of offensive or chemical type odor but I didn&#x27;t really detect Lavender either (and I use a LOT of lavender products so I am well acquainted with it).  My box came with a strip of plastic sealing tape pieces.  The plastic did feel very thin and I wouldn&#x27;t be comfortable walking around in just them or even propping them up for fear that the gel could leak out somehow.  Fortunately, I own a pair of large furry booty slippers that make me look like a muppet from the calf down so I slipped my bagged feet into those.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The instructions on MY box says to leave them on for only 1 hour.  Then wash feet with soap.  The dead skin cells will begin to peel 2-7 days after initial application.  I left product on for two hours after I knew that the amount of acid was reduced in this version.  I really don&#x27;t understand why the leave on time is LESS time with LESS acid ingredients?  You would think the less effective ingredient list would require MORE time on the feet.  Anyway, after two hours I removed the booties and washed my feet and thoroughly dried.  I didn&#x27;t feel any weird tingling or burning of any kind.  My feet did feel a bit warmer to the touch than usual however but that is probably because they were in baggies inside muppet slipper boots for two hours.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I dried my feet and didn&#x27;t apply any moisturizer of any kind at first.  The instructions do say that if your feet feel dry you apply a small amount of moisturizer.  It took 3 days to start noticing a bit of sloughing.  My feet didn&#x27;t get scaly but there was not a \\&quot;dramatic\\&quot; amount of peeling after 3 days.  It looks more like if you are in the tub 10 minutes too long and you start getting that whitish soft ring around the edge of the heel?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am writing this on day 3 because I wanted to get the differences of the product information out to you guys now.  I will be updating in about 3 more days and then give you my final thoughts/results after a full 14 days after the initial use of this product.  I will let you know what I am using in addition to this product in the next 11 days as well.  I am going to do nothing to one foot (as a \\&quot;control\\&quot;) and then if I use Shea Butter etc I will use it on the other foot exclusively.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT:  It has been 7 days since I first applied the product.  My heels feel like they are sore.  Not a burning sore just like if I have been standing all day.  My feet are finally starting to slough and peel.  However, only the tops of my feet.  A thin layer of skin can be peeled off much like the skin after a sunburn except there is no redness.  The bottoms of my feet are not visably peeling nor are they softer.  I suspect it is because the Baby Foot product I purchased is a different formula then the original Japanese product that comes in the box with the Japanese writing.  I have not tried the product packaged in the Japanese box but I know that there is far less acid in the Baby Foot product that I received.  I think this less acid is the reason there is no sloughing on the bottom of my foot.  The way the bag booties fit with the gel inside makes it impossible to concentrate the gel solely on the bottoms of the feet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT:  9 days after applying product.  I woke up this morning to the bottoms and sides of my feet finally peeling!  I am peeling off large pieces of skin to reveal new baby soft skin.  I had to scrape with my nail a bit to get the heel sections off but my skin didn&#x27;t tear like I was afraid it might.  So, it worked after all. It just took longer than I expected.  I do recommend this product but as others have mentioned, make sure you give yourself a good two weeks after initial application before you have to reveal your feet to anyone.  I would like to have the gel formula in a jar or bottle so that I could apply it to my heels only sometimes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT: Someone asked me today if I noticed my feet getting rough again after the initial effects of the treatment. YES. Two weeks after the initial smoothness (meaning after all the peeling was done) my feet were close to being right back to where they were before the treatment. This is why in my review I mentioned that it would be nice to have a bottle of the solution alone for periodic maintenance. I am back to having to apply creams such as shea butter nightly. As it stands now, plan on this method of softening to be for an event or vacation because it isn&#x27;t a long term solution.th soap.     <li> I was skeptical of this product since I have pretty thick calluses, but this product worked better than any pedicure I have ever gotten at a spa.  It was completely painless, my feet looked 100% better within a week, and it was cheaper than getting a spa pedicure.  That having been said, here are a few tips that I found that helped me get optimal results:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) Soak your feet in plain warm water before putting on the plastic booties.  Soak them for at least 15 minutes (longer if your feet are really rough, like mine were.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) Find a spot to sit in where you plan to hang out for awhile before you put the booties on.  Once they are on, they are really slippery and it is very hard to walk around.  Gather up all of the stuff you will want/need before you open the package.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) Open the booties and put them on one at a time.  The gel inside tends to leak out if you open the package and then lay the bootie down.  This mess can be avoided by putting one bootie on before cutting the second one open.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) Once the booties are on, put a thick pair of socks over the booties.  This holds the bootie on more securely and helps the gel penetrate your calluses more deeply.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5) The package says to leave the product on for only 30 minutes (I have seen on other reviews that some packages recommend 1-2 hours.)  To get the best results, decide how bad your calluses are, and then leave the booties on for the amount of time you need.  If you have nice, pretty feet, you won&#x27;t need to leave it on for more than an hour.  If you have nasty thick calluses like I did, you will want to leave the booties on longer.  I left the booties on for 6 hours with no side effects.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6) When it is time to take the booties off, wash your feet thoroughly with warm soapy water.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;7) Your feet will start to feel tight, like your skin is very dry.  This is totally normal and is part of the process.  DO NOT PUT LOTION ON - this will stop the peeling process and will defeat the whole purpose of the treatment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;8) Your feet will start peeling within 3-7 days, and will keep shedding dead skin for at least a week.  This is normal.  Do not apply lotion, or it will stop the process.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;9) As tempting as it may be, do not manually peel the skin off if it is not yet peeling.  This can damage the healthy skin underneath the dead skin.  Trust me, the dead skin will come off all by itself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;10) Each person is different.  Some shed skin in small pieces, while others have entire sheets of skin come off at once.  Be patient with the process.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;11) I applied this treatment to my feet about 5 days ago, and my feet are about 85% done peeling.  If you are doing this to prepare for a wedding/cruise/special event, give yourself ample time for the peeling process to complete.  Don&#x27;t apply this treatment just a few days before a big event, or you may still have ugly feet on the big day.  Give yourself at least two weeks for the process to be complete.process and will defeat the whole purpose of the treatment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;8) Your feet will start peeling within 3-7 days, and will keep shedding dead skin for at least a week. Everyone knows, or should know, that the whole pedi egg, scraping,filing, shaving etc. does little except prepare your feet for more hardened skin and callouses. Having once had a macho musician boyfriend who stood a lot at work and at gigs and had terrible feet and to whom I gave secret homemade pedicures using my own magic remedy and to my feet whose favorite activities are getting the paper on the driveway in the morning and walking all day everywhere in bare feet, my curiosity was piqued. It is pricey for what it is. I am not going to do the day by day results approach as this has been fairly well covered by other reviews; instead I am going to add a few tips of my own to the process, should you decide to purchase Baby Foot. First off, it is way overpriced for what it is, and no, the lavender aroma is hardly noticeable. So....have you ever marinated meat before cooking it to break down the sinewy veins etc. and open up its flesh? Well, same thing here. Wash your feet with soap, and dry. Do NOT apply lotion as this blocks the next step. Put a towel on the bottom of your container and fill it with water as hot as you can stand it. Add about a  cup of Epsom salts, white vinegar, pure cane sugar (this is the alpha hydroxyl acid ingredient mentioned in the product&#x27;s list), and baking soda. Do NOT add soap as it is a drying agent. Add lavender oil to get that psychological boost that you are being infused...after all you just spent @$25 for this indulgence to make yourself feel special with this one-time use product, and you do want to feel \\&quot;infused.\\&quot; Rub your feet against the towel as you soak for additional exfoliation, and when the water cools, remove your feet and dry them thoroughly. Again, do NOT apply lotion. Use the pricey product as directed...I also put plastic produce bags over the booties secured with rubber bands and tilted my feet at an angle so the gel would congregate around my heels, and I rested my feet on a dry towel just in case there was any leakage. After using the product...as you have read, there may be varying results...I purposely let my feet get real bad before I tested Baby Foot so as to give it a fair playing field. I wouldn&#x27;t recommend going to any soirees or events at which you will be exposing your feet as they will not be something anyone will want to see, and we ladies all know that we (and many men as well) always check out the footwear other women are wearing. Your feet at this stage will not be a thing of beauty that will be even promise to be a joy forever, and the gossip will be bursting at the seams. If you must reveal your feet however, apply and reapply a good sunscreen. Your skin is actually in a healing process, and like every peel process, the sun&#x27;s rays will cause damage. Do not go barefoot at all, for any reason, except in the shower or pool of course. There is dirt everywhere which will get in your healing skin&#x27;s pores, irritate it, and actually cause re-hardening (which yes, IS going to happen, even with Baby Foot.) While showering, use a pumice stone and a quality sugar scrub, and you know quality does not mean the Wallyworld&#x27;s sale item. Finally go to bed looking sexy, with a good shea butter slathered on and clean socks over this....which is also a good way to walk around your house too or to apply before putting on closed shoes. I would recommend Baby Foot if you really need to spend money on yourself in a manner that does not include buying a ten pack at the same price. Or you could just follow the marinating instructions above and apply a paste of the same cane sugar, a bottle of aspirin, (the salicylic acid),  apple, orange, lemon, and grapefruit juices, and baking soda, wrap up and make your own how-to You Tube video as you proceed. Most importantly, remember that this product, like any skin care one, is not a one time cure-all, and will need to be used repeatedly as maintenance. Overall, notworth the price....obviously a LOT of their profit is going into advertising.worth the price....obviously a LOT of their profit is going into advertising.</li>

    <li> We discovered that if you do this, Baby Foot works perfectly:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Soak feet for about 15 minutes in plain water (in a large bowl or bucket or sink or bathtub: whatever holds warm water &amp; both your feet).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Use Baby Foot exactly as directed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. Wash feet with soap and water, rinse, then soak feet again in plain water for about 15 minutes.  So, schedule about 2 hours for the process listed in #1 through #3.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. If you don&#x27;t see any sloughing or peeling after 2 to 4 days, then soak feet for about 30 minutes in plain water.  When you take feet out of the water &amp; blot dry, you will definitely see sloughing &amp; peeling.  If you continue to soak for another hour then you will see even more sloughing and peeling that you can begin to rub off.  Sloughing &amp; peeling will continue well-enough for several days without further soaking, and most of the dead &amp; dry skin will come off, BUT&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. if you continue to soak your feet in plain water for 30 minutes to an hour every other day or so, you will continue to see even more sloughing and peeling up to about two weeks AND it will thoroughly remove ALL dead &amp; dry skin from your feet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Two friends &amp; I discovered this after we used Baby Foot once (we didn&#x27;t know about the above directions at that time), and Baby Foot worked perfectly for the one of us who takes daily body-baths (doesn&#x27;t shower), worked well-enough for the one of us who took daily showers &amp; occasional body-baths, and didn&#x27;t seem to work at all for the one of us who Only takes showers (never body-baths).  We were comparing notes a few days after we first used it, and the shower-only friend was complaining that it didn&#x27;t work at all, absolutely no peeling whatsoever, and her feet looked exactly the way they did before she used Baby Foot.  We carefully went over every detail about what we had each done to our feet since applying Baby Foot, and carefully went over the Baby Foot instructions, which included this one little item written only in the little Instruction Manual sheet included in the box, \\&quot;Note: We recommend taking a footbath to enhance the effects BEFORE (sic) and AFTER (sic) using this product.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So we got out a large bowl, filled it with water, and had our shower-only friend soak her feet for 30 minutes, and voila! the dead &amp; dry skin on her foot looked white &amp; \\&quot;loose\\&quot;, and she rubbed it with her finger and it started sloughing off. She put her feet back in the water &amp; soaked for another hour, and when she took them out &amp; blotted them with a towel there was peeling all over her toes and peeling &amp; sloughing on her heels &amp; the ball of her foot.  The shower-only fried didn&#x27;t soak her feet again, and after two weeks most of the dead &amp; dry skin had come off well-enough.  The other two of us soaked our feet every day (the bath-only friend) or every other day (the occasional-bath friend) for the next two weeks, and both of us ended up with every single bit of dead &amp; dry skin removed, and had completely baby-soft feet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At different times all three of us have used it a second time after the initial use (shower-only friend after 3 months, occasional-bath friend after 6 months, bath-only friend after 8 months), we all followed the above instructions including soaking our feet for about 30 minutes every other day for the following two weeks, and we all three had perfect results the second time. You do not want to use lotion. This product is going to make your feet dry out, that is what causes the peeling. So it may be uncomfortable, but suck it up and have some dry feet for a few days! The next day (Wednesday) I noticed that the areas that needed the most &#x27;work&#x27; were a bit more sensitive. Today (Thursday) I noticed that my feet looked noticeably worse. The heels were super dry and turning a white color. After my bath, I rubbed one heel gently and a giant, disgusting chunk of skin just fell off. I rubbed the rest of my foot (no scratching, no pulling) and my entire foot began to flake off bits of funky dead skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2 DAYS!!!!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I will update this in a few more days and give details on how long the process took for me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*UPDATE*&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s been30 minutes since I wrote my review. I went to bed and quickly realized that it is necessary to wear socks to bed when using this product! So gross, but it&#x27;s what I paid for. Also looking at my feet after they had totally dried out from my bath made me see exactly how much is peeling. The heels, balls of my feet and sides of my toes look like they have tiny bubble forming under them. Ewwwwww&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*Friday Night*&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is disgusting- in a good way? I absentmindedly reached down to scratch the bottom of my foot (did notice a slight itch today) and a huge panel of skin as long as my hand and half as wide came off like it was nothing. The terrible calluses on my heels and balls of my feet are peeling in gross thick layers. The ball under one big toe is not quite at the peeling point, but the rest of the area has peeled so much that the variance in thickness is visible to the naked eye. Plus today I started to see all the areas of my foot that I thought were &#x27;ok&#x27; start showing how gross they were without me knowing it!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The soaking is a must. The more you soak, the more peeling occurs. I will suggest that you refrain from peeling when you get in the tub if you are taking baths. In fact don&#x27;t touch your feet at all when you get in the tub. Either wait until the end of your bath and then sit outside of your bath and scrub your feet or shower and use a foot bath for foot soaking and scrubbing. There&#x27;s a lot of skin coming off and you don&#x27;t want it floating in your tub!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;**April 18 Update**&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After three weeks I thought that it must be finished. Most of the calluses were gone with the exception of a bit on the side of my big toes and the center line of the ball of my feet (those of you that frequently wear higher heels will know exactly what that line is) and I was VERY happy with that. It was by far better than any pedicure result I have ever had. I decided that my heel addiction had left my feet in pretty bad shape and that I would do a second packet in a month to get that last bit taken care of. The thing is...I still am seeing slight peeling.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s been over a month and while I don&#x27;t see peeling every day, and it usually is not much, I am still slowly losing that area by my big toes. I have made sure to use baths as opposed to showers at least three times a week and every time I am able to scratch a bit more off. I lost a huge chunk off the last of the callus on my right big toe today and (sorry, this is so very, very gross!!!) I had to clean out my nails 5 times just from scratching my feet after my bath! I don&#x27;t know if anyone else has had these type of long results or if it is just because I left the pack on longer and continued to soak weekly, but this is pretty phenomenal.     <li> .&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Five star product!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was a little afraid, after reading some of the reviews, when I received my order of Baby Foot. But not to worry!  I will order this again.  And again. And again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;SIZE: I also received a package with Japanese writing on it.  More importantly, at the top corner, it indicated it was a \\&quot;size M.\\&quot; I wear a size 10 shoe (well, what can I say, I have a big heart, you know).  One reviewer said she wears a size 9 and had trouble getting her foot into the bootie.  NO WORRIES HERE!  The booties are big enough for an American Size 10 Woman&#x27;s foot, though you still have to be careful putting them on due to the amount of gel inside.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PROCESS: I decided, also based on other reviews, to a) soak my feet for 15 minutes (which turned into 20 because I was catching up on phone calls) before putting on the booties and b) to soak in the booties for 2 hours, rather than the 30 minutes the box recommends. It&#x27;s true that you should be very careful walking in the booties, since the insides are slippery and could make you lose your balance.  Buyer beware! and use caution!  I put some acrylic socks on over the booties, and also wore my rubber-soled sheepskin bedroom slippers over that, and this stabilized things somewhat.  I still needed to step carefully, and so here I am, sitting for the next long stretch until I&#x27;m done \\&quot;soaking.\\&quot;  I think anyone using this product should plan to sit still with a good book or a laptop or TV while \\&quot;soaking.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After having the booties on for almost an hour, I felt a slight warmth or tingling in the outer part of my foot.  Nothing to be concerned about.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did read the review that said the woman&#x27;s box had gel with much less acid listed in the ingredients. Mine seems to be the original recipe, with glycolic acid listed as the fourth ingredient (after water, alcohol and isopropyl alcohol).  Lactic acid is fifth, salicylic acid is further down the line, followed by citric acid and malic acid.  Following those are the herbal ingredients that seem more soothing.  The box I received says nothing about being \\&quot;lavender scented,\\&quot; nor did I detect any scent remotely like lavender.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;MY EXPERIENCE WITH THIS PRODUCT: I never had much problem with callouses on my feet until I reached a certain...ahem...age.  Perhaps because my skin is not as moist as it used to be, or perhaps because I have fewer hormones, I have a greater problem keeping the callouses on my heels under control.  My weapon of choice has been one of those paddles you buy at the drug store with the pumice-like surface in two levels of roughness.  I used the higher level on my heels before showering, and always get a bunch of callous shavings off.  Then I put cream on my feet.  I have one frustrating area I can never get to sufficiently: an oval area in the center of the ball of my foot.  The \\&quot;pumice paddle\\&quot; tool doesn&#x27;t get to that area.  I&#x27;ve also used a Dremel with a smoothing head, and, while that works, it doesn&#x27;t get all of it.  I&#x27;ve tried cutting it, with some success.  And I&#x27;ve had the podiatrist remove it, which works best.  I&#x27;m hoping this treatment takes away all my callouses, completely.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE, 2 hours later:  I have now removed the booties and washed the gel off.  I already have quite a bit of softenED callous rolling off of my heels when I rubbed with the towel.  I&#x27;m pretty sure this much would not have come off after a two-hour bath soak, though the longest I ever soak for is about an hour.  I just haven&#x27;t seen it this soft after just a water soak, so I&#x27;m sure the gel is already working. It&#x27;s not a peeling or flaking at this point, just a good amount that rolled off with the toweling. I&#x27;m here with comfy clean socks on, just waiting for the miracle to happen.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE, Day 2: no peeling yet or shedding.  About 2 hours after I wrote the last update, I realized why some reviewers are saying the product made their feet \\&quot;worse.\\&quot;  My feet, especially at the problem callous areas on my heels and outer edges of the sole, started looking and feeling really rough.  Yesterday and today, the skin feels sort of stiff, and tingly almost to the point of sun-burny, probably because I left the stuff on for 2 hours.  But they don&#x27;t really hurt, just a strong tingly feel. I soaked my feet for about 10 to 15 minutes last night, and towelled them off, rubbing the skin well.  Not much came off.  The heels and sides still look rough today. Socks are necessary today, for sure.  Waiting patiently for the peeling to begin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE, Day 4: The tops of my feet are starting to peel.  Nothing on the rest of the foot, meaning the bottoms where the callouses are, where it&#x27;s really needed. I have soaked my feet for 20 minutes twice since using the product, most recently last night.  I have not used lotion, for fear it would interfere with the process.  I&#x27;m beginning to wonder if I will be one of those on whom this product does not work very well.  Wonder what will happen tomorrow.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE, Day 6: My feet started peeling seriously last night, the evening of my 5th day.  A couple hours later, they were absolutely shedding.  Huge strips of skin started sloughing off, on the tops of my feet and on the bottoms.  I did read the review suggesting you shouldn&#x27;t pull the skin off, but I could not resist.  I sort of wanted to control where all this skin was going to land.  I did not pull it off if it did not come easily.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Today, Day 6, the peeling and sloughing continues, though not as wildly.  My heels and that pesky oval callous on each of my insteps are still there, though better, and are rough, not \\&quot;baby-soft,\\&quot; and I am hoping I can look forward to more peeling in those sections.  Otherwise, I will do another session in a month or so - after whatever the recommended waiting time is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE, Day 7: Late yesterday, a few hours after writing the Day 6 update, I noticed the callouses on my heels were sort of crumbling, but not peeling off.  I decided to soak my feet again, and this time ran hot water into the tub.  It was warm enough that I had to put my feet in and out to get used to it.  After putting my feet in, I did cool the temp down by running some cold water, but still let the water be warm.  I soaked for 20 minutes, then toweled them, rubbing firmly with the towel.  The remaining callouses just rolled away, and I am left with beautiful feet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That being said, I am now noticing that some places on the heels still feel \\&quot;thick\\&quot;, though they look great.  Also, there is still a \\&quot;thicker\\&quot; area on the balls of my feet, in the center where that tough-to-reach callous was.  I think I had a lot more callous build-up than I ever realized.  I am definitely going to order another kit and do this again in a few weeks.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have to give this product all 5 stars. (I wish I could give it 6 stars.) It&#x27;s fantastic, and works just as promised.     <li> Baby Foot is an interesting product -- you put your feet into gel-filled plastic baggies shaped like little boots and tape them closed.  Put a pair of socks over the top to keep everything where it belongs.  An hour or so later, rinse the goop off your feet.  And stand by.  Within four or five days, patches of skin will start peeling off of your feet.  If you want, you can spend countless hours picking off dead skin, pulling it off in inch-wide strips.  Or you can just scrub it off with a washcloth or exfoliant scrub.  About a week later -- voila!  Baby Feet!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;During the one-week sloughing period, you feet aren&#x27;t going to look so good.  They may look like you have a nasty case of eczema or some bad infection.  Your feet will be scaly and flaky and not so pretty.  But bear with it -- they will look great in the end!  Another word of caution -- best not to try walking around much with the booties on.  The gel-filled plastic boot is like a little slippery slide under your feet and it is hard to get traction.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some people complained that this doesn&#x27;t do much.
